- Header true-centering (composable header only, `headerRootRender`/`headerPuckConfig`): a Grid column set to "Centre" (`col*Align: 'center'`) or a 3-item space-distributed Group (`justify` between/around/evenly) centres its element on the header's own centre line via a header-scoped `position:absolute; left:50%` `<style>` rule emitted by `GridBlock`/`GroupBlock`. **Fixed 2026-07-08**: `GridBlock`'s column wrapper divs now carry an explicit `gridColumn: i+1` - without it, a centred (absolutely-positioned) middle column was skipped by CSS Grid's auto-placement, so any later column (e.g. a "Right" one) collapsed into the vacated track instead of holding its own position; reproduced live on the "Centred Navigation" starter header before the fix, confirmed resolved by DOM measurement after. Gated by the unconditional `data-header-root` marker on `headerRootRender`'s `<header>` plus its `position:relative` content wrapper (the absolute containing block); inert in the footer/page content where that marker is absent. Group's "exactly 3 items" gate is pure CSS (`:nth-child(2):nth-last-child(2)`) as the item count isn't reachable in render. NOT visually confirmed (static checks only).
- SiteLogo sizing: the logo `<img>` height comes from a shared `--header-cell-height` custom property set by the `cellHeight`/`cellHeightShrunk` fields ("Element height"/"Element height when shrunk", renamed from `logoHeight`/`logoHeightShrunk`); the shrink override swaps the property under `HEADER_SHRUNK_SELECTOR`. `SiteLogoClient` (editor) and `SiteLogoRsc` (live) both fall back to the old `logoHeight`/`logoHeightShrunk` keys, so `SiteHeaderBlock` (passes `logoHeight`) and pre-rename saved data need no migration. `scripts/migrate-sitelogo-cell-height.mjs` is a dry-run-default cleanup remap, not applied.
- RichTextBlock styling (2026-07-14, extended 2026-07-15): `richTextColourCss(id, { textColor, linkColor, linkHoverColor, bulletIcon, bulletColor })` (exported from `config.tsx`) emits a scoped `.puck-richtext[data-richtext-id="<id>"]` `<style>` block from BOTH the editor render (`RichTextBlock` in config.tsx) and the published render (`RichTextBlockRsc` in config.rsc.tsx, which imports the helper) so they stay identical. **Signature changed 2026-07-15** from `(id, colour)` to `(id, opts)` - only two call sites, both updated. Rules generated: `textColor` recolours `p,ul,ol,li,h1..h6,blockquote` (leaves links alone by design); `linkColor` → `a{color}`; `linkHoverColor` → `a:hover{color}`; `bulletIcon` (select) → `ul{list-style-type:<glyph>}` from the hardcoded `RICH_TEXT_BULLET_ICONS` map (`RICH_TEXT_BULLET_OPTIONS` feeds the dropdown: default/circle/square/dash/arrow/chevron/check/star/diamond/dot - keyword or quoted-string glyph, ordered lists untouched); `bulletColor` → `ul li::marker{color}`. Stylesheet rules not inline styles: the `.puck-richtext …` rules in `app/globals.css` set explicit descendant colours a wrapper `color` couldn't beat. All colours run through `cssColourValue` (strips `[<>{};]`); bullet glyphs are hardcoded so nothing user-typed reaches `list-style-type`. Fields: `textColor`/`linkColor`/`linkHoverColor`/`bulletColor` are `SiteColourField allowManual` swatch pickers (defaults `''`), `bulletIcon` a select (default `'default'`). NO in-editor colour toolbar - these are block settings, not toolbar marks. The `richtext` field's mark toolbar IS extended (2026-07-15) via its `renderMenu` hook to add a Link button (`lib/puck/RichTextLinkMenu.tsx` `RichTextMenuWithLink`, wired on `content`'s field def and reached through the field-widget registry) - Puck's default toolbar omits the link control despite the Link mark being on. The RSC path's `withSafeRichText` swaps the richtext field for a textarea but keeps other fields (`...base.fields`), so all styling props carry through; `renderMenu` is editor-only and never runs on the RSC path.
- Section vertical padding "Full view height" (2026-07-14): `SECTION_PADDING_Y_OPTIONS` (= shared `PADDING_Y_OPTIONS` + `{value:'screen', label:'Full view height (100vh)'}`) is Section-only so CTABanner et al, which reuse `PADDING_Y_OPTIONS` + `PADDING_Y_MAP`, don't offer an option their render ignores. In `SectionBlock`, `screen` → `min-height:100vh` with the `lg` (6rem) padding as its spacing; `min-height` is emitted on EVERY breakpoint in the `responsiveMediaCssFor` decl (`auto` when not screen) because those media rules only fire when a breakpoint differs from desktop - without the explicit `auto` reset, a desktop `100vh` inline base would leak onto a narrower breakpoint that set a normal padding. Desktop base carries `minHeight` inline too.
- Section content vertical alignment (2026-07-14): `contentAlign` field, a responsive select (`ResponsiveSelectField`, top/middle/bottom, default top) on the Section block, sitting next to `maxWidth` in the sidebar. Applied to the inner content box (`[data-section-id]`), the same element that already owns the max-width/vertical-padding/min-height, so it works with "Full view height" (`paddingY: 'screen'`) - which is the case where a section actually has spare vertical room to distribute. `top` deliberately stays `display:block` rather than a flex column with `justify-content:flex-start`: block flow keeps the children's normal margin collapsing, so every Section saved before the field existed renders byte-identically; `middle`/`bottom` switch the box to `display:flex; flex-direction:column` and push the stack with `justify-content:center|flex-end`.
- Section "Edge to edge" width (2026-07-15): `maxWidth` gained an `edge` option (value `'edge'` → 100% width, listed after "Full bleed"). Every other width keeps the standing 1.5rem horizontal gutter; `edge` drops it to 0 for true edge-to-edge content (heroes, maps, full-width media). The gutter is now a per-breakpoint `pxAt(d)` helper (`pickResponsive(mwRv, d) === 'edge' ? '0' : '1.5rem'`), used in the same `responsiveMediaCssFor` call and desktop inline padding as `pyPad`, so a section can be edge-to-edge on one breakpoint only. "Full bleed" (value `none`) is unchanged - still 100% width WITH the gutter - so existing full-bleed sections don't re-flow. The declaration is folded into the SAME `responsiveMediaCssFor` call as padding/max-width/min-height (one rule per breakpoint), and every branch emits an explicit `display:` so a desktop `flex` can't leak into a breakpoint set back to `top`, the same leak the `min-height:auto` reset guards against.
- Section border resolveFields fix (2026-07-14): `borderStyle: 'none'` now also strips `borderColor` + `borderWidth` from the sidebar (previously they showed regardless). Border radius stays visible either way - it rounds the section's background/image even with no border. The trim composes with the pre-existing background-mode trim (both run in one `resolveFields`, mutating a shared `result`).
- SiteLogo alignment (2026-07-14): `align` field, a responsive select (`ResponsiveSelectField`, left/center/right, default left) rendered via `lib/puck/siteLogoAlign.ts` - `LOGO_ALIGN_OPTIONS` + `siteLogoAlign(id, align)` returning `{ justifyContent, css }`. The helper is a shared module *precisely because* `SiteLogoClient` (editor) and `SiteLogoRsc` (live) are two separate implementations of the same markup ("Mirrors SiteLogoClient exactly") and are therefore a standing drift hazard - both call it, so the two halves cannot disagree. No wrapper element: the logo's `<a>` is already a block-level flex container (`display:flex`), so it spans the width it is given and `justify-content` moves the logo inside it; the desktop value is the inline base and tablet/mobile ride a per-instance `<style>` keyed on `a[data-sitelogo-id="<id>"]` via `responsiveMediaCssFor`. Unset resolves to `flex-start`, which is what the `<a>` already did (`justify-content`'s initial `normal` behaves as `flex-start` in a flex container), so backfilling the `left` default into pre-existing blocks is a no-op - and unlike `cellHeight` above, `align` has no legacy key for the backfill to shadow. Inside a header column the `<a>` is a flex *item*, sized to its content, so there is no free space to distribute and the field is inert there; header placement stays the column's own alignment setting. `SiteHeaderBlock` renders `SiteLogoRsc` directly with neither `id` nor `align`, which the helper handles (no `data-sitelogo-id` attribute, no emitted CSS).
- Responsive (per-breakpoint) field values: beyond Grid columns + MenuBlock nav, ~25 CSS-mappable fields (alignment, text/icon/logo size, gap, vertical padding, max-width, min-height, thickness across Heading/TextBlock/Caption/Section/Spacer/Divider/Split/Grid/Group/Hero/SocialLinks/Trustline/Logos/Copyright/ButtonLink/SiteLogo - the last two added 2026-07-14) store a `ResponsiveValue<T>` and render per breakpoint via `responsiveMediaCssFor` + `pickResponsive` (`lib/puck/responsiveValue.ts`): a per-instance `<style>` keyed on Puck's `id` (a `data-*` attribute on the block root), emitting `!important` `@media` rules at 640/1024 only when tablet/mobile differ from desktop - so legacy flat data renders byte-identically. Fields that size per-item children drive them through a shared custom property (`--social-icon`/`--logo-h`/`--copy-fs`). Field UIs: `ResponsiveSelectField`/`ResponsiveNumberField`/`ResponsiveTextField` (`ResponsiveValueField.tsx`, sharing `ResponsiveFieldShell`) and the generic `ResponsiveCustomField` (`ResponsiveCustomField.tsx`, atomic per-breakpoint object). MenuBlock's `alignment`/`spacing`/`itemFontSize`/`itemFontWeight`/`textTransform` are now `ResponsiveValue<string>` via `ResponsiveSelectField` too (desktop base inline, tablet/mobile as `!important` @media rules - horizontal path keyed on the ul's `data-menu-id`/`.cactus-nav-link`, vertical path on the existing `menu-vlist-shrink-<id>`/`menu-vlink-shrink-<id>` classes; font-size media skipped when the fluid clamp owns it, gap media skipped when fluid item spacing does). Content/URL/variant/colour/boolean/animation fields, Grid `col*Align`/Group `justify` (header-centring reads them in JS), Split `ratio`, and SiteLogo dimension fields are intentionally left flat/deferred. NOT visually confirmed (static checks only).
- Shared field helpers: `paddingField` (padding presets), `aosFields`/`aosDefaults` (AOS scroll-animation type/duration/delay on visual blocks), `SiteColourField` (site-palette colour picker fetching `/api/admin/appearance`).
- Editor-only field overrides applied in the editors (not in the base config): `OgImagePickerField` (root OG image, stores Media id) + the media-library picker applied via the shared `withImagePickerFields(config)` helper (`lib/puck/MediaPickerField.tsx`), which swaps every known image URL text field in a config for `ImageUrlPickerField` in one place - covers `ImageBlock`/`Card`/`ImageChipPanel` `mediaUrl`, `Hero` `bgImage` + `imageUrl` (side image), and `Section` `bgImage`; both `PuckEditor` (pages) and `LayoutPuckEditor` (layouts/header) run their config through it, so a new image field only needs adding to the helper's `IMAGE_PICKER_FIELDS` map. `MenuCheckboxField` (page menu assignment), `MenuSelectField` + `MenuBlockEditorPreview` (MenuBlock). The shared `MediaPickerModal` now browses folders: it fetches the folder tree from `/api/admin/media/folders`, shows a breadcrumb + clickable subfolder tiles, and scopes its media fetch to the current folder (`?folder=<id|root>&type=image`) - previously it called `/api/admin/media?perPage=50` with no `folder` param, which `parseLibraryQuery` treats as root-only (`folderId: null`), so any image organised into a folder was invisible in the Puck picker. Search now spans every folder server-side (`?folder=all&q=…&type=image`, 250ms debounced) instead of the old client-side filter over the 50 loaded root items.
- Both `app/cactus-admin/pages/[id]/PuckEditor.tsx` and `app/cactus-admin/layouts/[id]/LayoutPuckEditor.tsx` fetch `/api/admin/appearance` on mount and inject the site's real `buildTokenStyles`/`buildFontHref` (`lib/design/tokens.ts`) as a `<style>`/`<link>` into `document.head` - without this the canvas only inherits the admin shell's own `buildAdminThemeStyles` (just its `--color-primary` family), so token-driven props (`--btn-bg`, heading/caption font tokens, image border/radius tokens) render wrong in the editor even though they're correct live. The pages editor was missing this injection until 2026-07-04 - button variants that read `--btn-bg` (ButtonLink `primary`) rendered as the admin's own colour instead of the site's configured button colour. **Leak caveat:** this injected `<style>` sets `:root{…--radius-lg: 9999px…}` (site large-radius default from `buildTokenStyles`' `fixed` string), which clobbers admin globals.css's own `:root --radius-lg: 12px` for the whole document. Admin chrome that portals to `document.body` (the `NotificationBell` `.admin-bell-dropdown`) therefore inherited the pill radius and rendered as a circle on editor pages. Fix: admin chrome uses a dedicated `--admin-radius-lg` var (globals.css `:root`, 12px) that the token injector never emits, so it stays put.
- Data shape read/written: Puck `Data` JSON (`{content: Block[], root: {props}, zones}`). Storage fields - `InfoPage.builderData` (working draft, written by autosave), `InfoPage.publishedData` (live copy, written only by the publish endpoint), `InfoPage.history` (previous published blobs, cap 10), `Layout.builderData` (working draft), `Layout.publishedData`/`publishedAt`/`publishedById`/`history` (mirrors InfoPage's publish/archive pattern, written by the layouts PATCH route when `status: 'published'` is set). Page metadata (title/slug/status/metaDescription/ogImageId/menuIds) is mirrored into `root.props` for editing and reconciled back to real columns on save; `status` in root.props is never trusted from the client.
- Editor left sidebar: both editors pass a `plugins` prop to `<Puck>` (`@puckeditor/core`'s extension point - a `Plugin` with `label`/`icon`/`render` becomes a new sidebar tab, added alongside the built-in Blocks/Outline tabs; `usePuck()` inside a plugin's `render()` gives `{appState, dispatch, selectedItem}`, root props are edited via `dispatch({type:'replaceRoot', root})`). Shared factory `lib/puck/tabs/createPanelPlugin.tsx`. Tabs: Settings (`PageSettingsTab`/`LayoutSettingsTab`), SEO (`SeoTab`, pages only), Conditions (`DisplayConditionsPanel`, layouts only - previously injected via an `overrides.fields` hack, now a real tab), History (`PageHistoryTab`, reused for both pages and layouts), Saved Blocks (`SavedBlocksTab`, both editors - saves the `usePuck().selectedItem` snapshot to the `SavedBlock` table, re-inserts via a `dispatch({type:'insert'})` immediately followed by `dispatch({type:'replace', data: {...snapshot, props:{...snapshot.props, id}}})` to land the saved props under a freshly-generated id, mirroring Puck's own internal `insertComponent` helper. **Both dispatches target `destinationZone: 'root:default-zone'`** - Puck's `rootDroppableId` (`rootAreaId` `'root'` + `rootZone` `'default-zone'`); an earlier bare `'default-zone'` never matched the insert reducer's `zoneCompound === action.destinationZone` check, so Insert silently did nothing).
- Outline sidebar drag-and-drop (both editors, since 2026-07-14): Puck's own Outline tab is select-only - its `Layer` rows are plain `<button>`s with no dnd hooks, so blocks could only be rearranged by dragging on the canvas. Replaced by `lib/puck/outline/OutlineTree.tsx`, wired as `overrides.outline` in both editors. `overrides.outline` is a **wrapper** around Puck's default `LayerTree` (Puck renders `<Wrapper>{<LayerTree/>}</Wrapper>`), so the override simply ignores its `children` and renders its own tree instead. Rules of the road: (1) the tree is built from **public app state only** (`usePuck().appState.data` + `config`) - Puck's `state.indexes` is private and unavailable through `usePuck`, so `lib/puck/outline/tree.ts` walks `data.content` (root), slot props (any config field with `type: 'slot'`, e.g. `Columns.col1`), and legacy `data.zones` (the `puck.renderDropZone` API, still used by `Split`). Zone compound ids are `${parentId}:${slotOrZoneName}`, root is `root:default-zone`. (2) Reordering dispatches Puck's `{type: 'move', sourceZone, sourceIndex, destinationZone, destinationIndex}` - **within one zone Puck removes before it inserts**, so an insertion point below the item's current slot shifts up by one (`computeMove` in `tree.ts`, unit-tested in `tree.test.ts`). (3) Hover-highlight and scroll-to-block parity is kept without importing internals: Puck attaches its own `mouseover`/`mouseout` listeners to each canvas element and tags it `data-puck-component="<id>"` inside the `#preview-frame` iframe, so the outline dispatches synthetic `MouseEvent`s at that element rather than reaching for Puck's private `ZoneStore`. (4) Drops into the dragged block's own subtree are refused (`zoneIsInsideItem`), which is what stops a container being dropped inside itself. Drag is hand-rolled on pointer events (no dnd-kit dependency): 4px threshold for mouse, 220ms hold for touch so the panel still scrolls, Escape cancels, hovering a shut container for 500ms opens it, and the panel autoscrolls near its edges. Alt + arrow keys move a focused block (up/down within its zone, left out to the parent, right into the previous sibling's first slot), so reordering is not mouse-only.
- Editor chrome, both editors: page/layout no longer wrap `<Puck>` in their own topbar (back link, name, status badges, delete button). Instead: (1) `overrides={{header: createBackLinkOverride(backHref, label)}}` (`lib/puck/tabs/headerBackLinkOverride.tsx`) overlays a back-arrow link into the blank gutter Puck's own header already reserves left of its title on desktop (`_PuckHeader`'s `padding-left`, matching the pluginbar's width) - see `.cactus-puck-back-link` in `sidebarOverrides.css` (hidden below Puck's own 638px breakpoint, since that gutter doesn't exist on mobile and the link would overlap the mobile header's own content). (2) `<Puck headerTitle={...}>` sets what Puck's header shows instead of falling back to its default "Page" - layouts pass `getLayoutTypeLabel(layoutType)` (`lib/layout/layout-type-labels.ts`, since layout root props have no `title`), pages need no override (Puck's own fallback already reads the page's real title via `root.props.title`). (3) Name/description/priority/status live in `LayoutSettingsTab` (status is a plain draft/published `<select>`, PATCHing `{status}` directly - the same API-side publish/archive/display-conditions-validation logic in the layouts PATCH route fires regardless of whether `status: 'published'` arrives via this dropdown or Puck's own Publish button); title/slug/status/delete/preview live in `PageSettingsTab` (Delete opens the confirm-modal owned by `app/cactus-admin/pages/[id]/page.tsx`, Preview links to `/page-preview/[id]`). Saving/error feedback that used to live in the removed topbar now renders inline in `LayoutSettingsTab`; `PuckEditor.tsx` (pages) keeps its own inline status strip (saving state, publish errors, Published badge, "View live page" link) below the header, unaffected by this change.
- `_PuckLayout` (Puck's own root layout element) hardcodes `height: 100dvh`, assuming it always fills the full device viewport. Both editors nest it below other chrome (previously the removed topbars; still true generally for any future wrapper), so the real box it sits in is shorter - Puck rendered oversized regardless and the wrapper's `overflow: hidden` clipped the excess off the bottom, silently truncating the right sidebar's field list with no way to scroll to the missing part. Fixed by forcing `height: 100%` on `[class*="_PuckLayout_"]` in `sidebarOverrides.css` (imported by both editors) so it fills its actual parent box.
- Page resolution/rendering: public pages call `renderInfoPageContent` (`lib/puck/renderInfoPage.tsx`) - published pages render `publishedData` (fallback `builderData`), drafts render `builderData`; an `infoPage` Layout is resolved via `resolveThemeLayout` and the page content is injected into the layout's `ContentSlot` (`renderLayoutWithContent`). Markdown-format pages render sanitised HTML inside the same layout mechanism, then run `obfuscateEmailsInHtml` over the result (obfuscate-after-sanitise order invariant - see Email spam-protection).
- Layout resolution: `resolveThemeLayout(type, ctx)` picks the highest-scoring published Layout whose `displayConditions.include` matches the render context; exclusions veto. Scores: page_id 100, page_slug 90, homepage/not_found/coming_soon/maintenance 80, module 50, path_prefix 40, entire_site 10; ties broken by `priority` then `updatedAt` ordering.
- Server-side data resolution before render: `resolveTemplateData` deep-clones the blob and injects live values - MenuBlock/SiteHeader get resolved menu trees (`resolveMenu`/`resolveMainMenu`), SiteLogo/Copyright get siteName/logoUrl/year, LoginButton gets isLoggedIn/adminPath.
- **Changed 2026-07-08**: no background autosave in either Puck editor - content only writes to the DB on an explicit Update/Publish click (was: pages 1.5s debounce → `/autosave`; layouts 1.2s debounce → layout PATCH). Both editors track a local "unsaved changes" flag: warns via `beforeunload` on a real navigation/reload/close, and via a `confirm()` on the in-app "Back to Pages"/"Back to Layouts" link (`createBackLinkOverride` in `lib/puck/tabs/headerBackLinkOverride.tsx`, which a client-side `<Link>` nav would otherwise skip past unnoticed). `doAutosave`/the layout PATCH endpoint themselves are unchanged and still used by explicit actions (Update, History restore). **Fixed 2026-07-08**: `hasUnsavedChanges` was originally threaded into `createBackLinkOverride` as a plain boolean, which meant both editors' `puckOverrides` `useMemo` needed it in their deps - it flips false→true exactly once (the first real edit after page load), which recreated the *entire* overrides object and made Puck reinitialise mid-edit (reported as: first field edit after load kicks focus out and scrolls the sidebar to the top; every edit after that is fine, since the flag never flips again until the next Update/publish resets it to false). `createBackLinkOverride` now reads `hasUnsavedChanges` via a React Context (as of 2026-07-14 `EditorDirtyProvider`/`useEditorDirtyState` in `lib/puck/tabs/editorDirtyState.ts`, formerly `UnsavedChangesProvider` in this file) instead of a constructor argument, so the override factory call - and thus `puckOverrides`'s identity - no longer depends on it at all; the override component just reads the live value on its own render. (Two earlier attempts - a mutable ref read inside the click handler, then a `useCallback` wrapping that ref - both got flagged by the `react-hooks/refs` lint rule, which treats any ref-derived value passed into a function called during render as unsafe regardless of when it's actually invoked.) Publish flows: pages via `/publish` (history snapshot), layouts via PATCH `status: 'published'` (requires include rules).
- Module-declared layout types (generic mechanism, first used by Directory/Gazette/Boards, later also Shop): a module manifest can declare `layoutTypes: { groupLabel, types: [{key, label, starterImport?, starterExport?}] }`, extending the core `Layout.type` enum (`header|footer|infoPage|notFound|statusPage|<module-type>`) with camelCase types like `directoryCategory`/`directoryEntry`/`shopProduct`. `scripts/generate-module-layout-types.mjs` collects these into two gitignored files: `lib/layout/module-layout-types.ts` (`moduleLayoutTypeGroups`, `moduleLayoutTypeToGroup` lookup) and `lib/setup/module-starter-layouts.ts` (`moduleStarterLayouts: Record<type, () => Template[]>`). `puckBlocks[]` entries gain an optional `layoutTypes: string[]` tag (a block can be tagged into more than one type - e.g. Shop's `ShopProductGrid` serves `shopIndex`/`shopCategory`/`shopCollection` at once, `ShopUpsellProducts` serves both `shopProduct`/`shopCheckout`); `scripts/generate-module-puck.mjs` additionally buckets tagged blocks into `moduleComponentsByLayoutType`/`moduleRscComponentsByLayoutType` (both exported from `lib/puck/module-components.ts` alongside the existing flat maps - purely additive, untagged blocks are unaffected). `lib/puck/config.tsx`'s `getModuleLayoutPuckConfig(type)`/`getModuleLayoutPuckRscConfig(type)` build a scoped Puck config per module layout type: that type's tagged blocks plus the shared layout/typography/actions/media/content categories (deliberately excludes site/members - chrome-only concerns). The admin Layouts list/wizard (`app/cactus-admin/layouts/{page,new/page}.tsx`) render one extra top-level tab per module group, with a second-level `TabStrip` for that group's sub-types (e.g. Directory → Category/Entry, Shop → Shop Home/Category/Collection/Product/Checkout/Confirmation) when selected - **but only for modules the site has actually installed**. The two generated files above list every module the *build* cloned, which is every module in `modules.json`, on every install; the tabs are fed instead from `lib/layout/installed-layout-types.ts` `getInstalledModuleLayoutGroups()` (`Module.status IN ('active','update_available')` - the same gate the admin sidebar applies to nav entries), resolved by the server shell `app/cactus-admin/layouts/layout.tsx` and passed to the two client screens via `components/admin/ModuleLayoutGroupsContext.tsx` (`useModuleLayoutGroups()`). `isInstalledLayoutType()` is the matching server gate on `POST /api/admin/layouts` + `PATCH /api/admin/layouts/[id]`. `isKnownLayoutType()` stays build-time on purpose - an existing module layout must still open in its editor. `LayoutPuckEditor.tsx` and `app/layout-preview/[id]/page.tsx` fall back to `getModuleLayoutPuckConfig`/`Rsc` for any type found in `moduleLayoutTypeToGroup`; `DisplayConditionsPanel.tsx` offers only `entire_site` for unmapped types (one shared template per type, no per-instance targeting yet). Module starter templates are **not seeded at setup** - they are offered in the new-layout picker like core's, and nothing on a module's pages changes until the owner creates a layout from one and publishes it (most module pages already render a fully-working hardcoded fallback). A template can set `publishByDefault: true` to have `seedModuleDefaultLayouts(db, name)` create one ordinary published `<template-id>-live` Layout **when that module's install deploy lands** (`markModulesDeploySucceeded()`, guarded once by `Module.layoutsSeededAt`), for a module page with **no** hardcoded fallback - Shop's `shopIndex`/`shopProduct`/`shopCheckout`/`shopConfirmation` are Puck-only end to end (formerly served by Shop's own now-retired single-layout table), so exactly one starter per type sets this flag and the storefront keeps working out of the box, same principle as core's header/footer. Seeding cannot happen any earlier than that deploy: a module's code only reaches the build with it, so until then its templates do not exist to copy. (Before 2026-07-14 this ran inside `seedDefaultLayouts` at **setup**, when a site has *no* modules installed at all - which is how every fresh install ended up with Shop cart/checkout/product layouts in its database whether or not it had a Shop. `seedDefaultLayouts` is now core-only.) Layouts belonging to a module the site does not have are deleted by `pruneUninstalledModuleLayouts()` - from `ensureLayoutsCurrent()` (once per core version) and on uninstall; "does not have" means **no `Module` row AND no `ModuleMigration` rows**, so a `code_only` uninstall (which keeps both the module's tables and its migration ledger for a reinstall) keeps its layouts too. A module's `lib/starterLayouts.ts` **must stay pure data** (no server-only imports): core's picker imports the merged catalogue in the browser to draw each template's preview. Content-rendering model: the module's public page calls `resolveThemeLayout(type, ctx)`, and if a layout is published, clones `builderData` and injects live request context (slug/id/filter values) into specific tagged blocks' props via a per-module `lib/inject-*-context.ts` helper (the pattern this mechanism generalises from - Shop's original, module-specific `injectProductContext` - now itself just one more per-type helper alongside `inject-category-context.ts`/`inject-collection-context.ts`), then renders with `<Render config={getModuleLayoutPuckRscConfig(type)}>` - otherwise falls through to the original hardcoded JSX byte-for-byte (Shop's Category/Collection pages only - its other four types have no hardcoded path left to fall back to, see publishByDefault above).
- Email spam-protection (auto, published site only): every email address an owner puts on a page is obfuscated on the live site but stays plain in the editor (`!puck.isEditing`), via `lib/email-obfuscate.tsx`. Two techniques combined: the *visible* address is emitted as numeric HTML entities, so a bulk harvester scanning raw HTML for an "@" finds nothing; and the clickable `mailto:` href is never in the served markup at all - the address rides in a `data-eml` attribute (base64 of the reversed string) which `components/EmailDeobfuscator.tsx` decodes after hydration and turns back into `href="mailto:…"`. Two surfaces are covered:
  - **Text an owner typed** - *every* block, not just the five dedicated text ones. `linkifyEmails` returns `<ObfuscatedEmail>` nodes (Heading, TextBlock, Quote, Caption); `obfuscateEmailsInHtml` rewrites text runs for RichTextBlock; and `protectText(text, obfuscate)` (a thin gate over `linkifyEmails`, in `config.tsx`) covers the free-text props on every other block: CTABanner heading/subtext, Hero heading/subheading, Card heading/body, Callout title/body, ImageBlock caption, Eyebrow, Trustline, Chip label/value, Badge, Accordion answers, Stats value/label, FeatureList title/description, SpecPanel title/rows/badges, Ticker phrases, Copyright text. Two special cases: Accordion *questions* use `maskEmailText`, not `linkifyEmails` (a click anywhere in a `<summary>` toggles the panel, so a real link there would open the mail app *and* fold the answer away); and Chip takes an explicit `obfuscate` prop, because ImageChipPanel renders it from a plain array field with no `puck` to read.
  - **Links an owner pointed at their inbox** - `emailSafeHref(href, obfuscate)` (spread in place of `href={…}`) and `maskEmailText(label, obfuscate)` (for label text sitting *inside* the anchor, which can't be linkified - a nested `<a>` is invalid HTML). Applied to every block carrying an owner-typed href: ButtonLink, CTABanner, Hero (both CTAs), Card, Copyright (footer links), SocialLinks, Logos, linked Heading, and menu items (all four anchors in `MenuBlockClient.tsx`, which obfuscates unconditionally - it has no access to Puck's editing flag and needs none). A literal `mailto:` in an href is the single easiest thing on a page for a harvester to grep, so this was the biggest hole while it was open.
  - `obfuscateEmailsInHtml` tracks three contexts: ordinary text (wrap in a protected anchor), inside `<a>` (entity-mask the text only, and swap a hand-written `href="mailto:…"` for `data-eml` via `protectMailtoAttr`), inside `<code>/<pre>` (leave verbatim - a code sample is not a contact detail).
  - **Not covered, and can't be**: `alt`/`title`/`aria-label` attributes. React escapes attribute values, so an entity-encoded address would render as the literal text `&#64;`. Attributes are the hard edge of this technique. Also skipped: the sign-in/register labels on the Members blocks (owner-typed, but an address there isn't a real scenario, and the RSC mirror in `MembersBlocksRsc.tsx` would have to move in lockstep).
  - No-JS visitors still read the entity-encoded address (just not clickable). Editor keeps the raw address so it stays editable. `a[data-eml]{cursor:pointer}` in `globals.css` keeps a protected button looking clickable in the moment before the JS lands (no href means no pointer cursor from the UA stylesheet).
  - `lib/email-obfuscate.test.ts` guards the lot - the core assertion is "no '@', no `mailto:`, no address in the rendered markup". A regression here type-checks, lints and renders perfectly; the only symptom would be a quiet rise in the owner's spam, so nothing else in the toolchain can catch it.
  - **Order invariant with the sanitiser**: on the published RichText path, sanitise FIRST, obfuscate AFTER (`sanitizeAndObfuscateRichText` in `lib/sanitize.ts`, used by `RichTextBlockRsc` in `config.rsc.tsx`). DOMPurify parses and re-serialises its input, which decodes numeric entities - so obfuscate-then-sanitise silently puts the plain address back into the served HTML. `lib/sanitize-obfuscate.test.ts` guards the order (and proves the wrong order leaks).
  - **Module client props are a third surface**: anything passed as a prop to a `'use client'` component lands verbatim in the RSC flight payload, i.e. in view-source. The contact-form block leaked `notificationEmail`/`ccEmails` this way until 0.1.28 (`ContactFormPublicConfig` display subset now crosses the boundary; the submit route re-derives the full config server-side from stored block props). Same audit applies to any new module block: never hand a client component a config object with addresses in it.

### GitHub API Integration

Client resolution (`lib/github/client.ts`): GitHub App installation token (from the `GithubAppConnection` row, private key decrypted with ENCRYPTION_KEY) → `GITHUB_API_TOKEN` PAT → throw "not configured". `getGithubToken()` returns a bearer token for raw fetches; `getAppOctokit()` gives app-level JWT auth.

**A connection row is not a connection.** `loadConnection()` resolves one of four states - `none`, `unreadable` (row present, but this install's ENCRYPTION_KEY cannot decrypt its private key), `not-installed`, `ready` - and only `ready` authenticates. `unreadable` is the normal state after restoring a backup onto a fresh install, because setup mints a new ENCRYPTION_KEY per site and the backup's ciphertext was written under the old one. Treating "a row exists" as "connected" is what made a restored site report GitHub as set up and then fail every call with OpenSSL's `Unsupported state or unable to authenticate data` (surfaced as "Update failed: ..." and "Failed to load module directory"). `getGithubConnectionStatus()` exposes the state to the admin UI; `GET /api/admin/github-app` returns `connected` (ready or not-installed), `unreadable`, and `hasInstallation`. Anything reading a stored secret it did not write must use `tryDecryptSecret()` from `lib/crypto/secrets.ts`, never `decryptSecret()`.

Octokit endpoints called:

- `repos.listForOrg` - module directory listing (org `cactus-foundation-modules`).
- `repos.getLatestRelease`, `repos.listReleases` - module and core update checks (public vs beta channels); `git.getRef`/`git.getTag` to resolve release tags to commit SHAs.
- `repos.getContent` - read `modules.json`, `.gitmodules` existence; raw `raw.githubusercontent.com` fetch (with bearer token) for `cactus.module.json` manifests, guarded by strict `parseGitHubRepo` hostname validation.
- `git.getRef`, `git.getCommit`, `git.getBlob`, `git.createBlob`, `git.createTree`, `git.createCommit`, `git.updateRef` - Git Data API commits: module registry sync (`syncModulesJson`, commit message `chore: sync module registry\n\n[cactus-deploy]`, also deletes a legacy `.gitmodules`) and core updates (`syncCoreFromUpstream`: raw tree-diff of upstream tags - no ancestry assumption - copying changed core files into the admin repo, skipping `modules/`, `.gitmodules`, `modules.json`; upstream bytes read via `git.getBlob` by sha, no 1 MB cap; text files inlined into the tree via the `content` field so their blobs are written atomically with `createTree` - dodging the blob-replication race that surfaced as `GitRPC::BadObjectState` - and only binaries go through `createBlob`; optional modules.json pin in the same commit; BadObjectState retry with backoff on the residual binary path).
- `apps.getInstallation` - resolve the installation account after install.
- Raw REST (fetch): `POST /app-manifests/{code}/conversions` (App creation), `PUT /app/logo` (logo upload with app JWT).

Credential storage/encryption: the GitHub App's private key, webhook secret, client id/secret are AES-256-GCM encrypted (`lib/crypto/secrets.ts`, format `iv:authTag:ciphertext` hex) with `ENCRYPTION_KEY` and stored in the `GithubAppConnection` table - the stated single exception to "secrets live in env vars". The PAT alternative lives in the `GITHUB_API_TOKEN` env var.

### Media Layer

Provider types (`lib/media/providers.ts`):

- PROXIED (served via the Cloudflare Worker): B2, R2, S3, SPACES, WASABI, MINIO, VERCEL_BLOB, SUPABASE_STORAGE.
- DIRECT (own CDN + URL transforms; Worker never involved): CLOUDINARY, IMAGEKIT.
- Endpoint scheme tolerance: `B2_ENDPOINT`/`MINIO_ENDPOINT` are user-supplied and often pasted scheme-less (e.g. `s3.eu-central-003.backblazeb2.com`), which made the AWS SDK's internal `new URL()` throw `Invalid URL` and fail **every** upload (surfaced as "Upload failed: Invalid URL"). Both the Node upload path (`normalizeS3Endpoint` in `lib/media/upload.ts`, B2 + MINIO branches of `getS3Config`) and the Worker serving path (`normalizeEndpoint` in `workers/media-worker/index.ts` `fetchS3Compatible`) now prepend `https://` when no scheme is present (an explicit `http://` is kept for self-hosted MinIO). Fix applies at read-time so an already-stored scheme-less value works with no re-entry.
- Credential whitespace tolerance: S3 credential env vars (`*_ACCESS_KEY_ID`/`B2_APPLICATION_KEY_ID`, `*_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY`/`B2_APPLICATION_KEY`, `*_BUCKET_NAME`, `*_REGION`, `R2_ACCOUNT_ID`) pasted from a provider console often carry a trailing space/newline, which S3 request signing rejects (surfaced as "Upload failed: Malformed Access Key Id" for the key id, "SignatureDoesNotMatch" for the secret) and fails **every** upload/download/delete. `getS3Config` (`lib/media/upload.ts`) now reads every credential through `s3Env(key)` = `(process.env[key] ?? '').trim()`, so an already-stored tainted value works with no re-entry (read-time fix, mirrors the endpoint tolerance above). Write paths also trim before storing so nothing dirty is persisted again: `POST /api/admin/env` and `POST /api/setup/configure-env` now `.map(({key,value}) => ({key, value: value.trim()}))` instead of trusting the client-side trim in `ConfigPageClient.tsx`.
- The PROXIED/DIRECT distinction is app-code only, never a DB column. `SiteConfig.mediaProvider` selects the active provider for new uploads; each Media row records the provider it actually lives on.
- Console help data (also `lib/media/providers.ts`): `PROVIDER_SETUP_LINKS` (per-provider `SetupLink[]` deep-linking each provider's own console for buckets/keys), `CLOUDFLARE_DASH_URL` (account-agnostic `?to=/:account/workers-and-pages`), `CLOUDFLARE_API_TOKENS_URL` (`/profile/api-tokens`, where both the scoped token and Global API Key live), `CLOUDFLARE_TOKEN_PERMISSIONS` (the two scoped-token perms), `CLOUDFLARE_CREDENTIAL_KEYS`/`ALL_CLOUDFLARE_CREDENTIAL_KEYS` (Vercel env keys `CLOUDFLARE_API_TOKEN`/`CLOUDFLARE_GLOBAL_API_KEY`/`CLOUDFLARE_EMAIL`/`CLOUDFLARE_ACCOUNT_ID`), and `WORKER_SECRET_KEYS` (per-provider Worker secret names, mirrors the wiki's `wrangler secret put` list; empty for DIRECT; Vercel Blob uses `BLOB_BASE_URL` not the Vercel env token).
- Config Media tab (credentials card, proxied only) renders: a "Where to find these" link row; a **Set up the Worker automatically** box (paste a scoped API token *or* Global API Key + email + optional Account ID → `POST /api/admin/media/deploy-worker`), which uploads the Worker to the user's Cloudflare account and writes `CLOUDFLARE_WORKER_URL`; and a "Prefer to set it up yourself?" `<details>` fallback with a plain-English dashboard walkthrough (create Worker, Edit code, add Variables and Secrets, copy `.workers.dev` URL). No wrangler/terminal shown on screen.
- Auto-deploy internals: `lib/media/cloudflare-deploy.ts` (Cloudflare API client: `resolveAccountId` via `GET /accounts`, `uploadWorker` PUT multipart `main_module` + `secret_text` bindings, `enableWorkerUrl` claims/enables the `workers.dev` subdomain; auth = Bearer token OR `X-Auth-Email`/`X-Auth-Key`). Worker script uploaded is `cactus-media-worker`, compat date `2024-01-01`. Worker source is transpiled from `workers/media-worker/index.ts` to `lib/media/worker-source.generated.ts` (string export `MEDIA_WORKER_SOURCE`) by `scripts/generate-media-worker.mjs` (uses the `typescript` devDep; single-file type-strip, zero imports), run in `dev`/`build`, git-ignored via `.git/info/exclude`. Route `app/api/admin/media/deploy-worker/route.ts` (isAdmin, `maxDuration 60`) sources each `WORKER_SECRET_KEYS[provider]` value from the request body (freshly-typed) then `process.env`, derives `ALLOWED_ORIGIN` from `SITE_URL`, deploys, then persists the CF creds (two sensitive) + URL via `upsertVercelEnvVars` + `recordDeploymentNeeded`. `CLOUDFLARE_API_TOKEN`/`CLOUDFLARE_GLOBAL_API_KEY` added to `SENSITIVE_KEYS` (`lib/vercel/env.ts`); all four CF keys added to `ALLOWED_KEYS` (`app/api/admin/env/route.ts`).

Upload path (`lib/media/upload.ts`): 10 MB cap; JPEG/PNG/WebP/GIF only; sharp decodes the bytes and rejects content/type mismatches. S3-compatible providers use `@aws-sdk/client-s3` with per-provider endpoints; Vercel Blob via `@vercel/blob`; Supabase via `@supabase/storage-js`; Cloudinary/ImageKit via their SDKs (key = public_id / fileId). Object keys: `media/<PROVIDER>/<folderPath>/<nanoid>-<filename>.<ext>` (legacy B2 keys have no provider segment). `uploadMedia`/`relocateMediaBlob`/`buildKey` take an opt-in `exactName` flag: when set, the sanitised filename becomes the key basename verbatim with **no nanoid** (`…/<folderPath>/<name>.<ext>`) - the caller owns uniqueness within the folder. Used by the Shop's product-image filing (see Shop module) so image urls read `shop/<category>/<slug><n>.<ext>`; `moveOrRenameMedia` forwards the same flag. `organise.ts` also exports `getOrCreateFolderByPath(names[])` - walks/creates a folder chain by display name and returns the leaf folder id (idempotent), for auto-filing items into a known tree.

Cloudflare Worker (`workers/media-worker/index.ts`, excluded from tsconfig, deployed separately via wrangler): GET-only; validates `media/…` keys; infers the provider from the key path (unknown segment = legacy B2); fetches from the matching backend (SigV4-signs S3-compatible requests itself; Vercel Blob via BLOB_BASE_URL; Supabase via service-role REST); passes `?w=&q=` through Cloudflare Image Resizing options; responds with 1-year immutable cache headers and `Access-Control-Allow-Origin: ALLOWED_ORIGIN`.

URL construction/resolution: proxied rows store `<CLOUDFLARE_WORKER_URL>/<key>` as the canonical URL; direct rows store the provider CDN URL. The custom Next image loader (`lib/media/loader.ts`, wired via `next.config.ts images.loaderFile`) branches on hostname: Cloudinary gets `/upload/w_<w>,q_<q>/` inserted, ImageKit gets `?tr=w-…,q-…`, everything else gets `?w=&q=` appended for the Worker.

Migration (`lib/media/migration.ts`): one `MediaMigrationJob` at a time; 15-item batches; per item download original bytes → upload to destination → single-row provider/key/url update → best-effort delete of the original; failed items recorded and skipped by later batches; retry clears the failed list. Batches run only while an admin keeps the Settings → Media screen open (client loop), never via cron.

In-use computation (`lib/media/references.ts`): `loadMediaUsageIndex()` gathers, in one pass, every `Media.id` held in a FK column (`SiteConfig.logo/logoDark/favicon/faviconDark`, `InfoPage.ogImageId`, `Member.avatarMediaId`, `MemberDataExportRequest.mediaId`) plus a lowercased `haystack` of all Puck builder JSON (`InfoPage.builderData` + `publishedData`, `Layout.builderData`). `isMediaInUse(media, index)` returns true if the id is in the FK set OR the item's `url`/`key`/`id` appears in the haystack (Puck blocks embed media by url via bgImage/imageUrl/mediaUrl, or by id via ImageBlock/Card mediaId - stored in content, not as a relation). `getInUseMediaIds(rows)` classifies a batch. Consumed by the media library tabs and by `getMediaReferences` (`lib/media/upload.ts`) for delete warnings.

`saveMediaRecord`'s `uploadedById` is now optional (was required) - Member-uploaded avatars (MEMBERS_SPEC.md) have no valid value for it, since that column is a FK to the core `User` table and a `Member` is an entirely separate one.

Member avatars (Phase 4 of MEMBERS_SPEC.md, `Member.avatarChoice`): UPLOAD goes through the ordinary media pipeline above; GRAVATAR is served by `GET /api/members/avatar-proxy/[id]` - the server computes `sha256(email)` and streams the Gravatar bytes through this origin (24h cache) rather than redirecting to gravatar.com, so no CSP `img-src` addition is needed and the email/hash never reaches the client; GENERATED renders `components/members/GeneratedAvatar.tsx`, an inline SVG of the member's initials using `--color-bg-subtle`/`--color-border`/`--color-primary` (a single tone, not a per-user hue palette, to stay hardcoded-hex-free without inventing an avatar-specific colour list). `components/members/MemberAvatar.tsx` is the single dispatcher between the three, falling back to the generated avatar client-side if the Gravatar proxy 404s. Phase 9: `lib/members/avatar.ts`'s `resolveEffectiveAvatarChoice` downgrades a member's stored choice to whatever `avatarUploadsEnabled`/`gravatarEnabled` still permit, applied at every read (profile page, directory, account API, `MembersProfile` Puck block) and re-checked server-side in the avatar-proxy route itself.

Provider selection control: `SiteConfig.mediaProvider` (admin Settings → Media, persisted immediately); `isMediaProviderConfigured` requires every env var in `envKeysForProvider(provider)` (proxied providers include CLOUDFLARE_WORKER_URL). Uploads are refused until both hold.

### Email

- Provider chain (`lib/email/index.ts`): Brevo HTTP API when `BREVO_API_KEY` is set, else nodemailer SMTP (`SMTP_HOST/PORT/USER/PASS`); throws when neither is configured. From name/address come from `SiteConfig.emailFromName/emailFromAddress` (fallbacks: siteName / `noreply@example.com`). `SiteConfig.emailProvider` exists as a column but the chain is decided purely by env-var presence. `sendTestEmailWithCredentials(to, siteName, creds)` sends the standard test email through caller-supplied Brevo/SMTP credentials (unsaved form values; blank fields fall back to env) - used by the settings-page per-card "Send test email" button that appears next to "Save credentials" once new values are typed.
- Notification types sent by core (admin/User side): login OTP (password login), email verification code (registration), recovery link (recovery request), recovery-requested notice (same trigger), recovery-completed notice (recovery completion), password-changed notice (password add/change) - all plain `sendEmail` calls, no template override system.
- Module emails (contact-form): submission notification to the configured/admin address ("full" content or "notify"-only modes, optional CCs, reply-to submitter), auto-reply to the submitter (markdown with `{{name}}`/`{{email}}` placeholders), admin reply email (markdown + signature, reply-to the site address).
- In-app admin notifications (not email) live in the Notification table: "Changes awaiting deployment" (rolling, reasons deduped by label), `core-update`, `module-update:{id}`, `contact-form:messages` (rolling unread count); Members system re-uses the generic `message` type for pending-approval/deletion admin alerts (`lib/members/admin-notify.ts`, `upsertAlert` dedupe) - see below, it has no dedicated type of its own.

Members system emails (`lib/email/templates.ts`, admin-editable - see Phase 6 of MEMBERS_SPEC.md): 11 `member.*` templates, each with a code default and an optional `EmailTemplate` DB override (absence = default; reset = delete the row). Transactional ones (verify-email, magic-link, deletion-requested, deletion-cancelled, deletion-admin-notify, security-alert) always send; the rest (welcome, suspended, approved, digest-daily, digest-weekly) would check `MemberNotificationPreference` if the caller supplied a matching category, but core has no non-transactional categories of its own yet. `renderEmailTemplate(key, vars)` does `{{tag}}` interpolation (HTML-escaped in the body, plain in the subject); `sendMemberEmail(member, key, vars, opts?)` renders + sends via the ordinary `sendEmail`. Digests: `lib/members/digest.ts`'s `runDigest('DAILY'|'WEEKLY')` batches each member's subscribed-category `MemberActivityEvent` rows (by `type`) from the last 24h/7d into one email, cron-driven (`GET /api/cron/members/digest?mode=daily|weekly`, `CRON_SECRET`-gated).

### Scripts

- `scripts/migrate-sitelogo-cell-height.mjs` - one-off data migration + read-only audit for the SiteLogo "Element height" rename (`logoHeight`/`logoHeightShrunk` → `cellHeight`/`cellHeightShrunk`). Recursively walks `Layout` (type='header') `builderData`/`publishedData` and `SavedBlock` (componentType SiteLogo/Grid/Group) Puck blobs, remapping SiteLogo keys 1:1; also reports header true-centering coverage (centre-aligned Grid columns, 3-item space-distributed Groups). DRY RUN by default (reads, reports, writes nothing); `--apply` persists. Reads `DATABASE_URL` from `.env`. Not part of any build step; the render fallback makes it non-load-bearing.
- `scripts/migrate-grid-columns-split.mjs` - one-off data migration for the Grid component split (the single dynamic "Grid" Columns-select block replaced by fixed-column variants). Rewrites the affected Puck blocks across `Layout`/`InfoPage`/`SavedBlock` blobs. Reads `DATABASE_URL`; not part of any build step. Same non-load-bearing one-off shape as `migrate-sitelogo-cell-height.mjs`.
- `scripts/prebuild.mjs` - the single prebuild entry point for `npm run build` (`node scripts/prebuild.mjs && next build`). Replaces the old serial `&&` chain, whose real dependency graph is a fan-out rather than a line: `checkout-modules` must land module code on disk first (a barrier - everything downstream reads `/modules`), after which three branches run **concurrently** because none reads another's inputs or outputs - (a) `prisma generate`, (b) the database chain `build-migrate` → `sync-module-manifests`, (c) `generate-all`. `prisma generate` does not need the database, the migration chain does not need a generated client, and the generators need neither, so the prebuild costs the slowest branch rather than the sum. Each branch's output is buffered and flushed as one labelled block on completion (concurrent logs cannot interleave); any non-zero exit aborts the build with that branch's status, exactly as `&&` did. Also sets `CHECKPOINT_DISABLE=1` and `PRISMA_HIDE_UPDATE_MESSAGE=true` for every child, killing the Prisma CLI's version-check network round trip and its unactionable "update available" banner.
- `scripts/build-migrate.mjs` - conditional migration runner for Vercel builds. Skips entirely without DATABASE_URL; swaps Neon pooler URL for the direct endpoint (or DIRECT_URL); sets `PRISMA_SCHEMA_DISABLE_ADVISORY_LOCK=1` (plus `CHECKPOINT_DISABLE`/`PRISMA_HIDE_UPDATE_MESSAGE`, set here as well as in `prebuild.mjs` so a direct invocation behaves the same); runs `prisma migrate deploy`, then `reconcile-core-schema.mjs`, then `run-module-migrations.mjs`, each with 3 retries and backoff. Invokes the Prisma CLI through `node_modules/.bin/prisma` (falling back to `npx` only if that binary is absent) - `npx` re-runs npm's package resolution on every call for no gain. `migrate resolve --rolled-back` (which clears a failed-migration record left by an interrupted earlier apply, e.g. a Neon cold-start disconnect, that would otherwise block every later attempt with P3009) runs only **before a retry**, not before the first attempt: a stale failed record makes attempt 1 fail fast with P3009, the resolve then runs and attempt 2 applies cleanly, so recovery is unchanged while the happy path no longer pays a full Prisma CLI boot plus a DB round trip on every single build.
- `scripts/reconcile-core-schema.mjs` - build-step-only runner that closes core-schema drift on existing installs. The single core migration is edited in place and `prisma migrate deploy` never re-applies it, so additive changes made after an install was provisioned never reach its database. This runner applies every **unapplied** `.sql` in `prisma/core-reconcile/` (lexicographic) via a direct `pg` client (same SSL/direct-endpoint handling as `run-module-migrations.mjs`/`build-migrate.mjs`). Applied files are recorded, with their sha256, in the existing `ModuleMigration` ledger under the reserved module name `__core__` - deliberately not a new runner-owned table, which would show up in backups taken from one install and not another. Previously every file re-ran on **every** deploy for a guaranteed no-op; that list only grows, and each entry cost a statement batch and a database round trip per build. A file whose contents change is re-applied (checksum mismatch), so the self-heal guarantee is intact; an install predating the ledger simply applies each file once (a no-op on an up-to-date database) and records it. Each file is additive and idempotent (`IF NOT EXISTS` / `pg_constraint`-guarded FKs / `ADD VALUE IF NOT EXISTS`), so it is a no-op on fresh or up-to-date installs and adds only the missing objects on a drifted one. Skips without DATABASE_URL; 3 retries with backoff. Files: `001_media_folders_tags.sql` (Folder/Tag/MediaTag tables + `Media.originalName`/`folderId`/`optimised` columns and their indexes/FKs - the `/hq/media` crash on the deskwell install, 2026-07-11), `002_member_twofactor_phone.sql` (`MemberTwoFactor.phoneEncrypted`), `003_twofactor_sms_enum.sql` (adds `SMS` to the `TwoFactorMethod` enum - kept as the only statement in its own file because `ALTER TYPE ... ADD VALUE` cannot share a multi-statement transaction batch on older Postgres), `004_perf_indexes.sql` (the `Layout`/`Module.status` indexes, and drops three plain indexes duplicating a `@unique`), `005_retire_starter_layouts.sql` (deletes the legacy starter rows, *then* drops `Layout.isStarter` and its index - in that order), `006_module_layouts_seeded.sql` (`Module.layoutsSeededAt`, backfilled to `installedAt` for `active`/`inactive`/`update_available` modules only - one still mid-install or `failed` has never had its code in a build, so it stays NULL and is seeded when its deploy lands).
- `scripts/checkout-modules.mjs` - clones every `modules.json` entry into `/modules`, pinned to the recorded `version` tag (`git clone --depth=1 --branch`). On Vercel always a fresh clone; locally tries `git checkout HEAD -- .` in the existing clone first (this reverts uncommitted local edits to tracked module files). Modules are handled **in parallel** (each writes only its own directory and reads no other's, so the clones were never actually dependent - just serialised by the loop); each module's log lines are buffered and flushed as one block on completion so concurrent git output cannot interleave.
- `scripts/generate-all.mjs` - the single entry point `npm run dev` and `npm run build` use to run all eight generators below (router, puck, cron, settings-tabs, sms-providers, extension-points, layout-types, media-worker), in that order, in **one** Node process via sequential `await import()`. They were previously eight `&&`-chained `node scripts/generate-module-*.mjs` invocations, i.e. eight Node boots (one of them loading the whole TypeScript compiler for `generate-media-worker`) for a few hundred milliseconds of real work. Semantics are identical: same generators, same order, and a generator that calls `process.exit(1)` on a bad manifest (the duplicate-`publicBasePath` check in `generate-module-router.mjs`) still aborts the build. Add new generators to the END of the list, not the middle.
- `scripts/generate-module-router.mjs` - scans `modules/*/app/api/**/route.ts` and `modules/*/app/cactus-admin/<name>/**/page.tsx`; writes the gitignored `lib/modules/router.ts` (API dispatch table + lazy page loaders). For any module declaring `publicBasePath` in its manifest, also scans `modules/<name>/app/public/<base>/**/{page.tsx,route.ts}` and emits `resolveModulePublicPage`, `dispatchModulePublicRoute`, `getModulePublicBases`, and (if `modules/<name>/lib/sitemap.ts` exists, exporting `getPublicSitemapEntries(siteUrl)`) wires it into `collectModuleSitemapEntries`; fails the build if two modules declare the same `publicBasePath`. Runs on every dev start and build.
- `scripts/generate-module-puck.mjs` - collects `puckBlocks` from every module manifest; writes two gitignored files: `lib/puck/module-components.ts` (client-safe maps only) and `lib/puck/module-rsc-components.ts` (RSC maps only, server-only). Split into separate files (previously one) because a single shared file gave `lib/puck/config.tsx` a static import edge to any block's RSC half - if even one module block's RSC render used `next/headers` (e.g. Boards' cookie-based session checks), Next.js rejected the whole file the moment `lib/puck/config.tsx` was reached from the client Puck editor (`PuckEditor.tsx`/`LayoutPuckEditor.tsx`), regardless of which named export was actually used. Blocks whose RSC render needs server-only APIs must also split their own file in two (editor-safe placeholder + `.rsc.tsx` with the real render), and declare `rscImport` in the manifest pointing at the `.rsc` file (see `modules/boards/cactus.module.json`, `modules/gazette/cactus.module.json` for examples). RSC-only Puck config exports (`*RscConfig`, `getModuleLayoutPuckRscConfig`, `puckRscConfig`) live in `lib/puck/config.rsc.tsx`, not `config.tsx`, for the same reason.
- `scripts/generate-module-cron.mjs` - collects `cronJobs` from every module manifest; writes the gitignored `vercel.json` (`{crons: [...]}`); also prepends a hardcoded `CORE_CRONS` array (Members system: `/api/cron/members/purge`, `/api/cron/members/exports`) - core cron jobs are declared here rather than committed to `vercel.json` directly since that file is rebuilt from scratch on every build.
- `scripts/generate-module-settings-tabs.mjs` - collects `settingsTabs` from every module manifest (`{id, label, permission, import, component}`); writes the gitignored `lib/modules/settings-tabs.ts` (`moduleSettingsTabComponents: Record<id, Component>`). Consumed by `app/cactus-admin/config/ConfigPageClient.tsx` to render module-registered settings tabs generically (id/label/permission list comes from `app/cactus-admin/config/page.tsx`, which permission-filters live from `Module.manifest`, same pattern as `navEntries` in `layout.tsx`).
- `scripts/generate-module-sms-providers.mjs` - collects `smsProviders` from every module manifest (`{id, label, import, export}`); writes the gitignored `lib/modules/sms-providers.ts` (`moduleSmsProviders: Array<{module, id, label, provider}>`). Consumed by `lib/auth/sms.ts` (`getActiveSmsProvider()` - first configured provider from an active module, else null) to deliver login OTPs by text (admin password login + member SMS 2FA), always falling back to email.
- `scripts/generate-module-extension-points.mjs` - collects `extensionPoints` from every module manifest (`{point, id, permission, import, component}`); writes the gitignored `lib/modules/extension-points.ts` (`moduleExtensionPointComponents: Record<point, Record<id, Component>>`), grouped by the arbitrary `point` string. Core has no knowledge of any specific point name - a *publishing* module (e.g. `contact-form`) defines its own point names in its own page code and permission-filters live from `Module.manifest` (same pattern as `navEntries`/`settingsTabs`); a *contributing* module (e.g. `contact-form-reply-catcher`) declares entries against that point name in its manifest. See the "Module extension points" section in wiki/Authoring-a-module.md. First core (not module) publisher: `app/cactus-admin/config/page.tsx` (the Settings → Users → Roles subtab) reads `core.roles-page` the same way.
- `scripts/generate-module-layout-types.mjs` - collects `layoutTypes` from every module manifest; writes the gitignored `lib/layout/module-layout-types.ts` (pure data: groups + flat type→group lookup) and `lib/setup/module-starter-layouts.ts` (starter-template loader functions, imported per module). See "Module-declared layout types" under Puck Integration above.
- `scripts/generate-media-worker.mjs` - build-step: transpiles the Cloudflare media Worker (`workers/media-worker/index.ts`) to a plain ES module via `typescript` and embeds it as a string constant the app reads at runtime, so the admin > Settings > Media "Deploy Worker automatically" flow (`POST /api/admin/media/deploy-worker`) can upload runnable JavaScript to the user's Cloudflare account without a runtime transpile (`typescript` is a devDependency, pruned from the production runtime).
- `scripts/run-module-migrations.mjs` - build-step-only runner: for modules with status active/deploying/update_available, applies unapplied `modules/<name>/migrations/*.sql` files in lexicographic order, each in a transaction, recording name+checksum in `ModuleMigration`. The applied-migration ledger is read **once** into a Set up front, not one SELECT per (module, migration file) pair - with seven modules and several migrations each that was dozens of Neon round trips on every deploy purely to establish that there was nothing to do, which is the outcome on every build except the one that introduces a migration. The skip decision itself is unchanged.
- `scripts/sync-module-manifests.mjs` - build-step-only: rewrites `Module.manifest` from each deployed module's `cactus.module.json` so nav entries/teardown stay in step with shipped code. Skips without DATABASE_URL.
- `scripts/sync-wiki.mjs` - `npm run sync-wiki`: pulls all `.md` files from the GitHub wiki repo (`WIKI_SOURCE_REPO` or GITHUB_REPO + `.wiki`) into `/wiki` via the API.
- `scripts/fetch-google-fonts.mjs` - standalone maintenance script (own npm script, not in the build): fetches the Google Fonts metadata catalogue and writes `lib/design/google-fonts.json`, the source for the admin font pickers. Run manually to refresh the available-fonts list.
- `scripts/dev-warm.sh` - `npm run dev:warm`: kills anything on the port, clears `.next`, starts `next dev --webpack` (webpack chosen over Turbopack to avoid an HMR chunk-hash reload cascade), and pre-warms `/`, `/home`, `/logged-out`, `/setup`, `/style-guide`, `/privacy-policy` in the background.

Build-time order (from `package.json` `build`, which is now just `prebuild.mjs && next build`): checkout-modules, then three concurrent branches - (a) prisma generate, (b) build-migrate (migrate deploy → reconcile-core-schema → run-module-migrations) → sync-module-manifests, (c) generate-all (generate-module-router → generate-module-puck → generate-module-cron → generate-module-settings-tabs → generate-module-sms-providers → generate-module-extension-points → generate-module-layout-types → generate-media-worker) - then `next build`. Dev (`npm run dev`) runs the generators then `next dev --webpack`.

### Build and Deploy

- Build steps in order: see Scripts above. `npm run build` is the single entry; Vercel runs it on every push. It is `node scripts/prebuild.mjs && next build`, where the prebuild is `checkout-modules` (barrier) followed by `prisma generate`, the `build-migrate` → `sync-module-manifests` database chain, and `generate-all` running concurrently.
- **Turbopack's build filesystem cache is on** (`next.config.ts` → `experimental.turbopackFileSystemCacheForBuild: true`). It persists the compilation cache in `.next/cache`, which Vercel already restores from the previous deployment (the "Restored build cache from previous deployment" line in the build log). Without it the full Turbopack compile - 41s of a measured 103s deploy - was paid on every push regardless of how small the diff was. It is still flagged experimental in Next 16, so if a deploy ever produces stale or impossible output, this is the first thing to switch off.
- **`next build` does NOT type-check.** `next.config.ts` sets `typescript.ignoreBuildErrors: true`. Measured on a real Vercel build, the `tsc` pass inside `next build` was 26s of a 123s deploy, and it duplicated the `tsc --noEmit` gate that CLAUDE.md's work loop already requires on every change. The check moved, it was not dropped: **`npm run typecheck` is now the only thing standing between a type error and production**, so it is not optional before a commit. There is deliberately no CI workflow enforcing it - `lib/updates/core-plan.ts` excludes only `modules/`, `modules.json` and `.gitmodules` from the core-update push, so a `.github/workflows/*` file would propagate into every customer's repo and run CI on their GitHub account. Adding one means excluding `.github/` from the core sync first.
- Prisma migrations run only inside the Vercel build step (`build-migrate.mjs` → `prisma migrate deploy`), never at runtime; the advisory lock is disabled because Vercel serialises builds and Neon cold starts exceed the lock timeout. One migration file exists, edited in place for schema changes (fresh-install platform). Because migrate deploy never re-applies an edited-in-place migration, additive core changes reach already-provisioned installs via idempotent `prisma/core-reconcile/*.sql` run by `reconcile-core-schema.mjs` immediately after migrate deploy.
- `prisma db push` is blocked (`npm run db:push` exits 1 with a message).
- Vercel-specific: `vercel.json` is generated (cron entries only) and gitignored; deployments are auto-triggered by pushes to `main`; env-var-only changes use the redeploy API (`POST /v13/deployments?forceNew=1` based on the latest production deployment); module/core changes deploy via Git Data API commits (registry sync / core sync) whose push triggers the build; the redeploy gate (`pendingRedeployId` sentinel → real id → cleared on READY / webhook / dismiss / 4-minute server timeout) drives the admin shell's deploy status bar and the notification bell's live section meanwhile. Deployment status arrives via webhook (Pro) or lazy polling (`getLatestDeploymentStatus`, Hobby).
- jsdom is pinned to `^26` (jsdom 29 breaks the Vercel serverless update check with ERR_REQUIRE_ESM).
- Tester repo relationship: `usersaynoso/Cactus-Foundation-Tester` is a downstream install of this platform used for live testing; local `.env.local` points at the same Neon database as the live Tester site. Pushes to the Tester repo use the identity `Chris Taylor-Guest <airings.snug-0m@icloud.com>` and version-prefixed commit titles; core code reaches it via the in-app core-update sync (blob-level tree diff of core files vs the matching upstream tag, skipping `modules/`, `.gitmodules`, `modules.json`).
- Release flow (per CLAUDE.md): patch-only version bumps, tag format `vX.Y.Z`, GitHub release created immediately after every push.

### Slash Commands

None. `.claude/commands/` does not exist. `.claude/` contains only `settings.json` (permission allowlist + `caveman@caveman` plugin enablement) and runtime state files. Available slash commands come from installed plugins, not this repo.

### Utilities and Lib

`lib/` root:

- `deploy-log-translator.ts` - `translateLogLine(raw)`: maps Vercel build-log lines to friendly British-humour status messages (null = drop the line). Final line marker: "Bish bash bosh. You're live."
- `deploy-log-translator.test.ts` - vitest unit tests for the translator (run via `npm test`; no vitest config file exists).
- `markdown-client.ts` - browser-only markdown → sanitised HTML (marked + DOMPurify on `window`); identical allow-list to the server renderer.
- `sanitize.ts` - server/browser markdown → sanitised HTML; lazy-requires jsdom on the server; strips raw angle brackets pre-parse; also `markdownToPlainText`, `sanitizeRichText` (Puck RichText allow-list) and `sanitizeAndObfuscateRichText` (published RichText: sanitise first, obfuscate after - DOMPurify's re-serialisation decodes the obfuscator's entities, so the reverse order leaks the plain address; test: `lib/sanitize-obfuscate.test.ts`).
- `sanitize-config.ts` - shared `ALLOWED_TAGS`/`ALLOWED_ATTR` constants for both renderers.
- `email-obfuscate.tsx` - email spam-protection server half. `encodeEmail` = base64 of reversed address (the `data-eml` payload). For text: `linkifyEmails(text)` → React nodes (`<ObfuscatedEmail>` per match, entity-encoded visible text + `data-eml`); `obfuscateEmailsInHtml(html)` → same anchor markup spliced into text runs, entity-masking (not wrapping) inside `<a>`, rewriting a hand-written `href="mailto:…"` to `data-eml`, leaving `<code>/<pre>` verbatim. For owner-typed links: `emailSafeHref(href, obfuscate)` → `{href}` for ordinary links, `{'data-eml'}` and **no href** for a `mailto:` (query string preserved); `maskEmailText(label, obfuscate)` → entity-encoded `<span>` for label text inside an anchor, which can't be linkified without nesting an `<a>`. Consumed by every block in `config.tsx` (free text via the local `protectText` gate, hrefs via `emailSafeHref`) when `!puck.isEditing`, plus `MenuBlockClient.tsx`; client half is `components/EmailDeobfuscator.tsx`. Tests: `lib/email-obfuscate.test.ts`.
- `utils.ts` - `generateSlug`, `generateId` (nanoid), `parsePaginationParams` (page/perPage/skip, perPage ≤ 100), `errorResponse`, `successResponse`, `truncate`, `formatInTimezone`.

`lib/auth/`:

- `session.ts` - session + trusted-device create/validate/delete, cookie helpers, `listUserSessions`, `revokeSessionById`, `safeCompare` (timing-safe).
- `passkey.ts` - WebAuthn registration/authentication challenge creation and verification, `savePasskey`, `labelFromUserAgent`.
- `password.ts` - bcrypt hash/verify, strength check, Pwned Passwords check, `validateNewPassword`.
- `email-challenge.ts` - 6-digit OTP create/verify (10-min TTL, 5 attempts, hash compare).
- `rate-limit.ts` - action limits table (incl. Members system's `member_register`), `getClientIp`, `checkRateLimit`/`recordAttempt`, atomic `checkAndRecord` (raw INSERT … ON CONFLICT).
- `recovery.ts` - recovery token create/validate/consume (30-min TTL, single-use).
- `totp.ts` - secret generation, otpauth URI, QR data URL, `verifyTotpCode` with replay step guard.
- `turnstile.ts` - `verifyTurnstile` (fail-open unconfigured, fail-closed on error when configured).

`lib/config/`:

- `env.ts` - `isLocalMode`, `getEnvStatus` (single source of truth for the setup env-check and dashboard), `requiredEnvMissing`, `isEmailConfigured`, `isMediaProviderConfigured`, `getActiveMediaProvider`, `isMediaConfigured`, `configuredProxiedProviders`, `isGitHubConfigured`, `getGitHubConfigStatus`, `isVercelConfigured`, `isNeonConfigured`, `isEdgeConfigWritable`, `isTurnstileConfigured`, `getSiteUrl(+OrNull)`, `getWebAuthnRpId/Origin`, `getSessionSecret`.
- `site.ts` - 5-second in-memory caches for adminPath/status/pendingRedeployId (with the 4-minute redeploy auto-release), `invalidateSiteConfigCache`, `isSetupComplete`, the path/username BLOCKLIST, `isBlocklisted`, `generateSuggestedAdminPath`.
- `edge-config.ts` - Edge Config reads (`adminPath`, `siteStatus`) via `@vercel/edge-config`; `syncToEdgeConfig` writes via the Vercel REST API.
- `neon-regions.ts` - the 8 selectable Neon regions.

`lib/consent/`: `types.ts` (ConsentCategory/BannerConfig/Decision/CookiePayload + `DEFAULT_CONSENT_BANNER_CONFIG`), `gate.ts` (client: `hasConsent`, `onConsentChange`, `loadIfConsented`, `notifyConsentChange`; backs `window.cactusConsent`).

`lib/crypto/secrets.ts` - AES-256-GCM `encryptSecret`/`decryptSecret` using ENCRYPTION_KEY; format `iv:authTag:ciphertext` (hex).

`lib/members/`:

- `config.ts` - `MembersConfigSchema` (Zod, all Members settings with defaults: enabled false, registrationMode OPEN, emailVerificationRequired true, allowedAuthMethods [PASSKEY, MAGIC_LINK], passwordsEnabled false, trustedBrowserDays 30, sessionDays 30, avatar/gravatar toggles true, siteWideMembersOnly false + exceptions [], guestPreviewEnabled false, username changes off with 90/30-day cooldown/redirect, deletionGracePeriodDays 14, domain allow/blocklists [], profileVisibility PUBLIC, accountSectionsEnabled all true, directoryEnabled false, smsTwoFactorPolicy OPTIONAL - OPTIONAL|REQUIRED, whether members with a password must enrol a mobile number for SMS sign-in codes; REQUIRED only bites while an SMS provider module is active, see `sms-policy.ts` below), `parseMembersConfig` (corrupt column falls back to defaults), `getMembersConfig`, `getMembersConfigCached` (5s TTL for proxy reads), `invalidateMembersConfigCache`.
- `paths.ts` - `MEMBER_INTERNAL = '/cactus-account'`, `DEFAULT_MEMBER_AREA_PATH = 'account'`, `getMemberAreaPath()` (sanitised MEMBER_AREA_PATH env var; invalid or blocklisted values fall back to the default, `account` itself exempt from the blocklist check).
- `sms-policy.ts` - `memberNeedsSmsEnrolment(config, twoFactorConfigs)`: true only when `smsTwoFactorPolicy` is REQUIRED, the member has no verified SMS `MemberTwoFactor` row, AND an SMS provider module is active/configured (`getActiveSmsProvider`) - no provider means the policy silently behaves as OPTIONAL. Consumed by the password login + 2fa verify routes (`smsEnrolmentRequired` response flag → `LoginForm.tsx` `finishLogin` redirects to the account overview instead of `redirectTo`) and by the member account layout (warning banner, shown only to members who actually have a password).
- `tokens.ts` - hashed single-use tokens for member verification links (mirrors `lib/auth/recovery.ts`): `generateMemberToken`/`hashMemberToken`, `createVerificationToken`/`consumeVerificationToken` (`MemberVerificationToken`, 24h TTL), `canResendVerification` (60s per-member throttle, keyed off the latest token row regardless of used/unused).
- `registration.ts` - `isUsernameFormatValid`/`isUsernameAvailable` (format regex + blocklist + `Member.username` uniqueness), `isEmailDomainAllowed` (allow/blocklist against `membersConfig`), `deriveInitialStatus`/`deriveActivatedStatus` (status a `Member` is created with vs. the status it moves to once verified, per `registrationMode`; verification is only "required" when both `emailVerificationRequired` is true AND email is actually configured, otherwise there'd be no way to ever satisfy it), `validateInviteToken`/`consumeInviteToken` (`MemberInvite`, single-use), `sendVerificationEmail` (shared by the register route and the resend route), `loginRejectionForStatus` (single source of truth for every login method: null when a status may sign in (ACTIVE only), else `{error, redirectToVerify?}`).
- `session.ts` - member session/cookie layer, fully separate from `lib/auth/session.ts`: `createMemberSession`/`validateMemberSession` (ACTIVE-only, sliding expiry) /`deleteMemberSession`/`deleteAllMemberSessions`/`listMemberSessions`/`revokeMemberSessionById`, cookie helpers (`cactus_member_session`), `getMemberFromCookie`; trusted-browser twin `createMemberTrustedBrowser`/`isMemberBrowserTrusted`/`revokeAllMemberTrustedBrowsers` (cookie `cactus_member_trusted`). Durations read from `membersConfig.sessionDays`/`trustedBrowserDays` via `getMembersConfigCached`.
- `passkey.ts` - WebAuthn registration/authentication for members, mirrors `lib/auth/passkey.ts` against `Member`/`MemberPasskey`; reuses `WebAuthnChallenge` with `memberId` set and `member_registration`/`member_authentication` purposes instead of a second challenge table.
- `magic-link.ts` - `sendMagicLink`/`consumeMagicLink`, hashed single-use `MemberMagicLink` tokens (15-min TTL, plain sha256 like `tokens.ts` - status gating happens at the route, not here).
- `email-challenge.ts` - mirrors `lib/auth/email-challenge.ts` against `MemberEmailChallenge`; `createMemberEmailChallenge`/`verifyMemberEmailChallenge`, purposes `login_2fa`/`setup_2fa`, 10-min TTL, 5 attempts, hash compare.
- `recovery-codes.ts` - `generateMemberRecoveryCodes` (10 codes, shown once, replaces any unused set), `consumeMemberRecoveryCode`, `countRemainingRecoveryCodes`.
- `activity.ts` - `recordMemberActivity` (`source: null` = core, else the contributing module name), `listMemberActivity`.
- `deletion.ts` - `requestMemberDeletion`/`cancelMemberDeletion` (grace period from `membersConfig.deletionGracePeriodDays`), `purgeScheduledDeletions` (cron target, hard-delete past the grace period).
- `export.ts` - `assembleMemberExport` (core tables + each active module's `memberExtensions.dataExportPath`, called over self-origin HTTP with an internal bearer derived from `SESSION_SECRET` - `verifyInternalExportBearer` is exported for a module's own handler to check it), `createDataExportRequest` (assemble→upload→ready, synchronously within the request; refuses a second request while one is in flight; deletes the stuck row on failure rather than leaving it stuck, since the schema has no FAILED status), `expireDataExports` (cron target, 48h).
- `admin-log.ts` - `logMemberAdminAction(actor, memberId, action, detail?)`, writes a `MemberAdminActionLog` row (actor snapshot, not a live relation - survives the admin user being deleted later).
- `admin-notify.ts` - `notifyAdminMemberPendingApproval`/`notifyAdminMemberDeletionRequested`: in-app alert (reuses the generic `message` `NotificationType` + `upsertAlert` dedupe - members have no dedicated notification type of their own) + an email to every protected-role admin when email is configured (the deletion one renders through `lib/email/templates.ts`, `member.deletion-admin-notify`; the pending-approval one has no matching template in the 11-key registry, so it stays a plain inline send). Gating on `notifyAdminOnPendingApproval`/`adminNotifyOnDeletion` happens at the call site, not in here.
- `digest.ts` - `runDigest('DAILY'|'WEEKLY')`, see the Email section.
- `access.ts` - pure matching logic for `proxy.ts`'s Phase 8 site-access gate: `isPathExcepted`, `resolveRouteTier` (no I/O, unit-testable in isolation from the session/DB lookups that surround them in proxy.ts).
- `avatar.ts` - `resolveEffectiveAvatarChoice`, see Media Layer section.

`lib/db/prisma.ts` - global-singleton PrismaClient (query logging in development).

`lib/deploy/`: `reconcile.ts` (`markModulesDeploySucceeded` - promotes pendingVersion, clears alerts; `markModulesDeployFailed` - reverts to update_available or failed), `redeploy.ts` (`startDeferredRedeploy` - arms the redeploy gate synchronously, then in `after()` syncs modules.json or falls back to an env-var redeploy, and polls Vercel for the new deployment id).

`lib/design/tokens.ts` - `DesignTokens` v2 type, `DEFAULT_DESIGN_TOKENS`, `COLOUR_PRESETS`, `buildTokenStyles` (tokens → CSS custom properties for the public site), `buildAdminThemeStyles` (primary-colour family + `--font-sans` only, for admin white-labelling), `buildFontHref` (Google Fonts URL for non-system fonts).
